The statement of the prominence of the tunica uvea refers to the significance or importance of the tunica uvea, which is a crucial structure in the human eye. The tunica uvea, also known as the uveal tract, comprises three layers of pigmented vascular tissue: the iris, ciliary body, and choroid. These layers play essential roles in providing nourishment to the retina, regulating intraocular pressure, controlling the amount of light entering the eye, and supporting overall ocular function. The prominence of the tunica uvea lies in its integral involvement in maintaining visual acuity and protecting the inner structures of the eye from damage due to excessive light exposure or other stressors.

You're saying that bones look different when you see them in homes and in ruins, but it's not possible for them to be continuous and solidified according to their nature due to the drying out of their body parts. However, this statement is somewhat misleading. Bones indeed change over time, especially after decomposition begins, which involves moisture loss among other factors. But they are never truly "consolidated" or "solidified" in the way you're implying. Instead, bones undergo a complex process of mineralization and fossilization that can preserve them for long periods if conditions allow. So while there is some truth to your observation about their appearance change, the concept of continuous solidification isn't accurate.
